upper_32_bits(chip->corb.addr));\n738: \n739: \t/* set the corb size to 256 entries (ULI requires explicitly) */\n740: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBSIZE, 0x02);\n741: \t/* set the corb write pointer to 0 ICH6_CORBCTL_RUN);\n747: \n748: \t/* RIRB set up */\n749: \tchip->rirb.addr = chip->rb.addr + 2048;\n750: \tchip->rirb.buf = (u32 *)(chip->rb.area + 2048);\n751: \tchip->rirb.wp = chip->rirb.rp = 0;\n752: \tmemset(chip->rirb.cmds, 0, sizeof(chip->rirb.cmds));\n753: \tazx_writel(chip, RIRBLBASE, (u32)chip->rirb.addr);\n754: \tazx_writel(chip, RIRBUBASE, upper_32_bits(chip->rirb.addr));\n755: \n756: \t/* set the rirb size to 256 entries (ULI requires explicitly) */\n757: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBSIZE, 0x02);\n758: \t/* reset the rirb hw write pointer */\n759: \tazx_writew(chip, RIRBWP, ICH6_RIRBWP_RST);\n760: \t/* set N=1, get RIRB response interrupt for new entry */\n761: \tif (chip->driver_caps & AZX_DCAPS_CTX_WORKAROUND)\n762: \t\tazx_writew(chip, RINTCNT, 0xc0);\n763: \telse\n764: \t\tazx_writew(chip, RINTCNT, 1);\n765: \t/* enable rirb dma and response irq */\n766: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBCTL, ICH6_RBCTL_DMA_EN | ICH6_RBCTL_IRQ_EN);\n767: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n768: }\n769: \n770: static void azx_free_cmd_io(struct azx *chip)\n771: {\n772: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n773: \t/* disable ringbuffer DMAs */\n774: \tazx_writeb(chip, RIRBCTL, 0);\n775: \tazx_writeb(chip, CORBCTL, 0);\n776: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n777: }\n778: \n779: static unsigned int azx_command_addr(u32 cmd)\n780: {\n781: \tunsigned int addr = cmd >> 28;\n782: \n783: \tif (addr >= AZX_MAX_CODECS) {\n784: \t\tsnd_BUG();\n785: \t\taddr = 0;\n786: \t}\n787: \n788: \treturn addr;\n789: }\n790: \n791: static unsigned int azx_response_addr(u32 res)\n792: {\n793: \tunsigned int addr = res & 0xf;\n794: \n795: \tif (addr >= AZX_MAX_CODECS) {\n796: \t\tsnd_BUG();\n797: \t\taddr = 0;\n798: \t}\n799: \n800: \treturn addr;\n801: }\n802: \n803: /* send a command */\n804: static int azx_corb_send_cmd(struct hda_bus *bus, u32 val)\n805: {\n806: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n807: \tunsigned int addr = azx_command_addr(val);\n808: \tunsigned int wp;\n809: \n810: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n811: \n812: \t/* add command to corb */\n813: \twp = azx_readb(chip, CORBWP);\n814: \twp++;\n815: \twp %= ICH6_MAX_CORB_ENTRIES;\n816: \n817: \tchip->rirb.cmds[addr]++;\n818: \tchip->corb.buf[wp] = cpu_to_le32(val);\n819: \tazx_writel(chip, CORBWP, wp);\n820: \n821: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n822: \n823: \treturn 0;\n824: }\n825: \n826: #define ICH6_RIRB_EX_UNSOL_EV\t(1<<4)\n827: \n828: /* retrieve RIRB entry - called from interrupt handler */\n829: static void azx_update_rirb(struct azx *chip)\n830: {\n831: \tunsigned int rp, wp;\n832: \tunsigned int addr;\n833: \tu32 res, res_ex;\n834: \n835: \twp = azx_readb(chip, RIRBWP);\n836: \tif (wp == chip->rirb.wp)\n837: \t\treturn;\n838: \tchip->rirb.wp = wp;\n839: \n840: \twhile (chip->rirb.rp != wp) {\n841: \t\tchip->rirb.rp++;\n842: \t\tchip->rirb.rp %= ICH6_MAX_RIRB_ENTRIES;\n843: \n844: \t\trp = chip->rirb.rp << 1; /* an RIRB entry is 8-bytes */\n845: \t\tres_ex = le32_to_cpu(chip->rirb.buf[rp + 1]);\n846: \t\tres = le32_to_cpu(chip->rirb.buf[rp]);\n847: \t\taddr = azx_response_addr(res_ex);\n848: \t\tif (res_ex & ICH6_RIRB_EX_UNSOL_EV)\n849: \t\t\tsnd_hda_queue_unsol_event(chip->bus, res, res_ex);\n850: \t\telse if (chip->rirb.cmds[addr]) {\n851: \t\t\tchip->rirb.res[addr] = res;\n852: \t\t\tsmp_wmb();\n853: \t\t\tchip->rirb.cmds[addr]--;\n854: \t\t} else\n855: \t\t\tsnd_printk(KERN_ERR SFX \"spurious response %#x:%#x, \"\n856: \t\t\t\t   \"last cmd=%#08x\\n\",\n857: \t\t\t\t   res, res_ex,\n858: \t\t\t\t   chip->last_cmd[addr]);\n859: \t}\n860: }\n861: \n862: /* receive a response */\n863: static unsigned int azx_rirb_get_response(struct hda_bus *bus,\n864: \t\t\t\t\t  unsigned int addr)\n865: {\n866: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n867: \tunsigned long timeout;\n868: \tunsigned long || do_poll) {\n876: \t\t\tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n877: \t\t\tazx_update_rirb(chip);\n878: \t\t\tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n879: \t\t}\n880: \t\tif (!chip->rirb.cmds[addr]) {\n881: \t\t\tsmp_rmb();\n882: \t\t\tbus->rirb_error = 0;\n883: \n884: \t\t\tif (!do_poll)\n885: \t\t\t\tchip->poll_count = 0;\n886: \t\t\treturn chip->rirb.res[addr]; /* the last value */\n887: \t\t}\n888: \t\tif (time_after(jiffies, timeout))\n889: \t\t\tbreak;\n890: \t\tif (bus->needs_damn_long_delay || loopcounter > 3000)\n891: \t\t\tmsleep(2); /* temporary workaround */\n892: \t\telse {\n893: \t\t\tudelay(10);\n894: \t\t\tcond_resched();\n895: \t\t}\n896: \t}\n897: \n898: \tif (!chip->polling_mode && chip->poll_count < 2) {\n899: \t\tsnd_printdd(SFX \"azx_get_response timeout, \"\n900: \t\t\t   \"polling the codec once: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n901: \t\t\t   chip->last_cmd[addr]);\n902: \t\tdo_poll = 1;\n903: \t\tchip->poll_count++;\n904: \t\tgoto again;\n905: \t}\n906: \n907: \n908: \tif (!chip->polling_mode) {\n909: \t\tsnd_printk(KERN_WARNING SFX \"azx_get_response timeout, \"\n910: \t\t\t   \"switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n911: \t\t\t   \"disabling MSI: last cmd=0x%08x\\n\",\n919: \t\t\t   chip->last_cmd[addr]);\n920: \t\tfree_irq(chip->irq, chip);\n921: \t\tchip->irq = -1;\n922: \t\tpci_disable_msi(chip->pci);\n923: \t\tchip->msi = 0;\n924: \t\tif (azx_acquire_irq(chip, 1) < 0) {\n925: \t\t\tbus->rirb_error = 1;\n926: \t\t\treturn -1;\n927: \t\t}\n928: \t\tgoto again;\n929: \t}\n930: \n931: \tif (chip->probing) {\n932: \t\t/* The command was\n964:  *       intended for the BIOS only, and may get confused with unsolicited\n965:  *       responses.  So, we shouldn't use it for normal operation from the\n966:  *       driver.\n967:  *       I left the codes, however, for debugging/testing purposes.\n968:  */\n969: \n970: /* receive a response */\n971: static int azx_single_wait_for_response(struct azx *chip, unsigned int addr)\n972: {\n973: \tint timeout = 50;\n974: \n975: \twhile (timeout--) {\n976: \t\t/* check IRV busy bit */\n977: = -1;\n988: \treturn -EIO;\n989: }\n990: \n991: /* send a command */\n992: static int azx_single_send_cmd(struct hda_bus *bus, u32 val)\n993: {\n994: \tstruct azx *chip = bus->private_data;\n995: \tunsigned int addr = azx_command_addr(val);\n996: \tint timeout = 50;\n997: \n998: \tbus->rirb_error = 0;\n999: \twhile (timeout--) {\n1000: \t\t/* check ICB busy bit */\n1001: \t\tif azx_power_notify(struct hda_bus *bus, bool power_up);\n1062: #endif\n1063: \n1064: /* reset codec link */\n1065: static int azx_reset(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n1066: {\n1067: \tint = 1;\n1230: }\n1231: \n1232: /*\n1233:  * initialize the PCI registers\n1234:  */\n1235: /* update bits in a PCI register byte */\n1236: static void update_pci_byte(struct pci_dev *pci, unsigned int Returns non-zero if it's OK.\n2207:  *\n2208:  * Many HD-audio controllers appear pretty inaccurate about\n2209:  * the update-IRQ timing.  The IRQ is issued before actually the\n2210:  * data is processed.  So, we need to process it afterwords in a\n2211:  * workqueue.\n2212:  */\n2213: static int azx_position_ok(struct azx *chip, struct azx_dev *azx_dev)\n2214: {\n2215: \tu32 wallclk;\n2216: \tunsigned int pos;\n2217: \tint stream;\n2218: \n2219: \twallclk = azx_readl(chip, WALLCLK) - azx_dev->start_wallclk;\n2220: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 2) / 3)\n2221: \t\treturn -1;\t/* bogus (too early) interrupt */\n2222: \n2223: \tstream = azx_dev->substream->stream;\n2224: \tpos = azx_get_position(chip, azx_dev, true);\n2225: \n2226: \tif (WARN_ONCE(!azx_dev->period_bytes,\n2227: \t\t      \"hda-intel: zero azx_dev->period_bytes\"))\n2228: \t\treturn -1; /* this shouldn't happen! */\n2229: \tif (wallclk < (azx_dev->period_wallclk * 5) / 4 &&\n2230: \t    pos % azx_dev->period_bytes > azx_dev->period_bytes / 2)\n2231: \t\t/* NG - it's below the first next period boundary */\n2232: \t\treturn bdl_pos_adj[chip->dev_index] ? 0 : -1;\n2233: \tazx_dev->start_wallclk += wallclk;\n2234: \treturn 1; /* OK, it's fine */\n2235: }\n2236: \n2237: /*\n2238:  * The work for pending PCM period updates.\n2239:  */\n2240: static void azx_irq_pending_work(struct work_struct *work)\n2241: {\n2242: \tstruct azx *chip = container_of(work, struct azx, irq_pending_work);\n2243: \tint i, pending, ok;\n2244: \n2245: \tif (!chip->irq_pending_warned) {\n2246: \t\tprintk(KERN_WARNING\n2247: \t\t       \"hda-intel: IRQ timing workaround is activated \"\n2248: \t\t       \"for card #%d. Suggest a bigger bdl_pos_adj.\\n\",\n2249: \t\t       chip->card->number);\n2250: \t\tchip->irq_pending_warned = 1;\n2251: \t}\n2252: \n2253: \tfor (;;) {\n2254: \t\tpending = 0;\n2255: \t\tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n2256: \t\tfor (i = 0; i < chip->num_streams; i++) {\n2257: \t\t\tstruct azx_dev *azx_dev = &chip->azx_dev[i];\n2258: \t\t\tif (!azx_dev->irq_pending ||\n2259: \t\t\t    !azx_dev->substream ||\n2260: \t\t\t    !azx_dev->running)\n2261: \t\t\t\tcontinue;\n2262: \t\t\tok = azx_position_ok(chip, azx_dev);\n2263: \t\t\tif (ok > 0) {\n2264: \t\t\t\tazx_dev->irq_pending = 0;\n2265: \t\t\t\tspin_unlock(&chip->reg_lock);\n2266: \t\t\t\tsnd_pcm_period_elapsed(azx_dev->substream);\n2267: \t\t\t\tspin_lock(&chip->reg_lock);\n2268: \t\t\t} else if (ok < 0) {\n2269: \t\t\t\tpending = 0;\t/* too early */\n2270: \t\t\t} else\n2271: \t\t\t\tpending++;\n2272: \t\t}\n2273: \t\tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n2274: \t\tif (!pending)\n2275: \t\t\treturn;\n2276: \t\tmsleep(1);\n2277: \t}\n2278: }\n2279: \n2280: /* clear irq_pending flags and assure no on-going workq */\n2281: static void azx_clear_irq_pending(struct azx *chip)\n2282: {\n2283: \tint i;\n2284: \n2285: \tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n2286: \tfor (i = 0; i < chip->num_streams; i++)\n2287: \t\tchip->azx_dev[i].irq_pending = 0;\n2288: \tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n2289: }\n2290: \n2291: #ifdef CONFIG_X86\n2292: static int azx_pcm_mmap(struct snd_pcm_substream *substream,\n2293: \t\t\tstruct vm_area_struct *area)\n2294: {\n2295: \tstruct azx_pcm *apcm = snd_pcm_substream_chip(substream);\n2296: \tstruct azx *chip = apcm->chip;\n2297: \tif (!azx_snoop(chip))\n2298: \t\tarea->vm_page_prot = pgprot_writecombine(area->vm_page_prot);\n2299: \treturn snd_pcm_lib_default_mmap(substream, area);\n2300: }\n2301: #else\n2302: #define azx_pcm_mmap\tNULL\n2303: #endif\n2304: \n2305: static struct Let me look at the azx_init_chip function again and see if there's a problem with the initialization of the chip->initialized flag. In particular, when azx_init_chip is called during resume:\n\n```c\nstatic void azx_init_chip(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n{\n\tif (chip->initialized)\n\t\treturn;\n\t...\n\tchip->initialized = 1;\n}\n```\n\nThe issue is likely that after suspend/resume, the chip->initialized flag is still set to 1, so when azx_init_chip is called again in azx_resume, it returns immediately without actually reinitializing the chip!\n\nThis is a classic bug. During suspend, the chip is disabled but the initialized flag is not reset. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012E9zuybXcQFr5XEzCFzxQu","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I can see the structure. Key state fields:\n- `poll_count` (line 490) - used to track polling attempts\n- `initialized` (line 492) - whether the chip is initialized\n- `single_cmd` (line 493) - whether to use single command mode\n- `polling_mode` (line 494) - whether we're in polling mode\n- `rirb.cmds[addr]` and `rirb.res[addr]` - response tracking\n\nLooking back at the azx_init_cmd_io function (line 730-768), I can see:```c\nstatic void azx_init_cmd_io(struct azx *chip){\tspin_lock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n\t/* CORB set up */\t...\t/* RIRB set up */\n\tchip->rirb.addr = chip->rb.addr + 2048;\tchip->rirb.buf = (u32 *)(chip->rb.area + 2048);\n\tchip->rirb.wp = chip->rirb.rp = 0;\n\tmemset(chip->rirb.cmds, 0, sizeof(chip->rirb.cmds));  // <-- This line is important!\t...\tspin_unlock_irq(&chip->reg_lock);\n}```\n\nLine 752 is crucial: `memset(chip->rirb.cmds, 0, sizeof(chip->rirb.cmds));` - this clears the pending command counters.\n\nNow, the issue is becoming clearer. When the driver switches to single_cmd mode due to timeout:1. azx_free_cmd_io is called, which disables CORB/RIRB\n2. chip->single_cmd is set to 1\n3. chip->rirb.cmds[addr] is never reset to 0\n\nThen during resume:1. \n\nazx_init_chip is called, but it only invokes azx_init_cmd_io when (!chip->single_cmd). Since single_cmd mode was enabled, the initialization function skips the memset that would clear the command counters. This leaves stale values in chip->rirb.cmds, causing azx_rirb_get_response to incorrectly believe there are pending commands waiting for responses when there actually aren't.\n\nThe function checks if (!chip->rirb.cmds[addr]) to determine whether a response is ready, but with the old counter still set, it will timeout waiting for a response that will never arrive. The solution involves either clearing the rirb.cmds array explicitly during the mode switch, or resetting flags during resume to force a full CORB/RIRB reinitialization rather than skipping it.\n\nThe issue appears to compound across multiple suspend/resume cycles—the sound card gradually degrades until errors become noticeable. The core problem is that when falling back to single_cmd mode, the cmds array isn't cleared, leaving stale command counters that prevent proper operation if the driver attempts to return to CORB/RIRB mode or if the transition never completes cleanly.\n\nThere are three operational modes: normal CORB/RIRB communication, polling mode when responses lag, and single-cmd mode using direct I/O when CORB/RIRB times out. When switching to single-cmd, azx_free_cmd_io disables the RIRB but doesn't reset the cmds array, so subsequent suspend/resume cycles encounter leftover values that trigger timeouts. Alternatively, the chip->single_cmd flag itself might not be getting properly reset during resume, preventing the driver from attempting to re-enable CORB/RIRB.\n\nLooking at azx_init_chip, if chip->single_cmd is already set, it skips azx_init_cmd_io entirely—which works if staying in single-cmd mode is intentional, but the stale cmds array remains problematic. The real culprit appears to be chip->polling_mode never being cleared. After suspend/resume, if the driver entered polling mode due to timeout issues, that flag persists even though chip->initialized gets reset to 0. When azx_init_chip runs on resume, it re-enables interrupts, but the driver continues polling instead of using the restored interrupt-driven communication.\n\nThe core problem is that error recovery state like polling_mode doesn't get cleared during resume, preventing the hardware from getting a fresh start after power cycling. The driver should reset polling_mode to 0 in azx_resume to allow interrupt-based communication to work The azx_resume function does not reset chip->polling_mode to 0 before reinitializing the hardware, causing the driver to continue using polling mode instead of interrupts after resume. After a suspend to RAM and resume:\n- The driver remains stuck in polling mode instead of using interrupts\n- The driver remains in single-cmd mode instead of using the normal CORB/RIRB command I/O\n- The `rirb.cmds[]` array retains stale command counters from before the mode switch\n\nThis causes continued timeouts and the choppy audio symptoms reported.\n\n### **Why This Causes the Bug**\n\nAfter multiple suspend/resume cycles, if a timeout occurs even once, the driver switches to error recovery mode. Upon resume, these error recovery flags persist, preventing the driver from attempting to use normal communication methods again. The codec remains unresponsive because the driver is using degraded communication paths (polling/single-cmd) which are inadequate.\n\nThe fix would require resetting these flags in the `azx_resume()` function or in `azx_init_chip()` to give the hardware a fresh chance to operate normally after being power-cycled."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":792,"cache_read_input_tokens":67869,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":792},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3e8b5271-d38c-4196-a070-f23e254208c8","uuid":"37a1f9d3-46d4-451e-bcec-120d99f1ee0a"}
